غير اعتبار المعنى. كذا في البدائع ولهذا لو أوصى بثلث ماله للأصناف السبعة فصرف إلى صنف واحد لا يجوز، وقيل يجوز . كذا في المحيط.
Chapter of the Recipient: It is the poor (faqir) and the needy (miskin), and the needy is worse off than the poor, and the worker, the one whose contract (mukatab), and the debtor. The author did not restrict it to the recipients of zakat to include zakat, tithe, and the fifth of minerals as indicated in the conclusion. It is appropriate to give the fifth of minerals because its recipient is the spoils, as stated by al-Asbiji and others. The seven categories were mentioned and the 'authors of hearts' was omitted to indicate its abrogation due to the consensus of the Companions; it is of the type of termination of a ruling due to the termination of its absent cause for which payment was made, for payment was for honor, and Allah has honored Islam and made them independent. In al-'Inaya it was chosen that it is not abrogation because honor now is in not paying, so it is a confirmation of what was, not abrogation. It was objected to in Fath al-Qadir that this does not negate abrogation because the permissibility of paying to them was a legal ruling that existed and has been removed. They were three categories: a category given to incline their hearts to Islam, a category given to repel their evil, and a category who had embraced Islam but had weakness, so they were given to strengthen them. And it is not said that abrogation of the Book by consensus is impermissible because the abrogator is the evidence of consensus, not consensus itself, based on the fact that there is no consensus except from a source. If it appears, it must be ruled that the ruling is established, and the verse that 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) mentioned is suitable for that: 'And say, the truth is from your Lord, so whoever wills let him believe, and whoever wills let him disbelieve' (Quran 18:29). His saying: 'The poor is worse off and the needy is the poor' i.e. the recipients are the poor and the needy, and the needy is worse off. The difference between them is stated in al-Hidayah and elsewhere: the poor is one who possesses the least thing, the needy is one who has nothing. Some say the opposite, each has a face, and the first is the most correct and is the school. Thus in al-Kafi. It is better to interpret 'possessing less than the nisab' as in al-Niqayah, taken from their saying: It is permissible to give zakat to one who possesses less than the nisab or an amount of nisab that is not growing and is consumed by need. There is no dispute that they are two categories in zakat; this is correct because the conjunction in the verse necessitates difference. The dispute is only whether they are two categories or one category in other than zakat, such as bequest (wasiyyah), endowment (waqf), and vow (nadhr). Abu Hanifa held the first (two categories), and this is correct as in Ghayat al-Bayan; Abu Yusuf held the second (one category). So if one bequeaths one-third of his wealth to a specific person and to the poor and needy, according to the correct view, the specific person gets one-third of the one-third; according to the other view, he gets half of the one-third. The permissibility of giving zakat to a single category is for a reason not found in bequest: the fulfillment of need, and that is achieved by giving to a single category. Bequest was not legislated to fulfill the need of the legatee – it is permissible for a rich person as well, and the testator may have many intentions not known, so the text of his words cannot be explained by considering the meaning. Thus in al-Bada'i; therefore if one bequeaths one-third of his wealth to the seven categories and then gives it to a single category, it is not permissible; some say it is permissible. Thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage from Bab al-Masrif (Chapter on the Recipients) of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defines the primary recipients of zakat. The author, Imam Zain al-Din ibn Nujaim, explains that the 'needy' (miskin) is worse off than the 'poor' (faqir), which is the correct view in the Hanafi school. The distinction is based on ownership: the faqir owns some property but insufficient to meet his needs, while the miskin owns nothing. This difference is crucial for the distribution of zakat. The text also discusses the omission of the category 'mu'allafatu qulubuhum' (those whose hearts are to be reconciled), which was abrogated by the consensus of the Companions after the strength of Islam made them unnecessary. The author addresses the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether faqir and miskin are two separate categories for all charitable dispositions or only for zakat. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that they remain two categories for bequests, endowments, and vows, while Imam Abu Yusuf considers them one category. The practical effect is seen in bequests: if someone bequeaths one-third to 'the poor and needy' and another person, the shares differ depending on the view. This shows that the rule for zakat is not automatically transferred to other areas due to differing underlying rationales.

Key Terms
الفقير (al-faqir): One who possesses less than the nisab (minimum threshold) or an amount equal to the nisab but non-growing and entirely consumed by immediate needs.
المسكين (al-miskin): One who possesses nothing at all; worse off than the faqir.
المؤلفة قلوبهم (al-mu'allafatu qulubuhum): Those whose hearts are to be reconciled; a category of zakat recipients that was abrogated by consensus after Islam became strong.
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest made by a person during his lifetime to take effect after his death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school as affirmed in this passage, which of the two—faqir or miskin—is considered worse off (aswa' halan)?
A) Al-faqir
B) Al-miskin
C) Both are equal
D) It depends on the context

Key Takeaway
The conjunction in the zakat verse ensures that faqir and miskin remain distinct categories for all legal purposes, according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Conditions for a Creditor to Receive Zakat
Ruling on zakat eligibility for creditors, with expansions from later sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine when a person owed a debt may validly receive zakat, distinguishing between deferred and immediate debts, and apply the ruling for a woman owed prompt dower, including the precautionary fatwa.

Core Idea
A creditor can take zakat only if the debt is practically unrecoverable, like deferred debts or an insolvent debtor.

This lesson examines the detailed conditions under which a person who is owed money (the creditor) can receive zakat. The ruling hinges on whether the debt is deferred (future due) or immediate, and whether the debtor is wealthy, insolvent, or denies the debt. A special case involves a woman whose husband owes her prompt dower (mahr), where the scholars differed on the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of debt
First, determine if the debt is deferred (due later) or immediate (due now). This classification is the foundation of the ruling.
Deferred debt = the creditor cannot demand immediate payment; immediate debt = the creditor can demand payment at any time.
2
Check the debtor's financial status and cooperation
For immediate debts, examine if the debtor is insolvent (cannot pay), wealthy and admitting, wealthy and denying with witnesses, or denying without witnesses. Each scenario yields a different ruling on the creditor's eligibility for zakat.
The passage analogizes an insolvent debtor to ibn al-sabil (wayfarer), making zakat permissible.
3
Apply the special dower (mahr) ruling
If the creditor is a woman owed prompt dower by her wealthy husband, consider the husband's willingness to pay. If he would pay on demand, zakat is not allowed; if he would not pay (even though wealthy), it is allowed, due to the difficulty of suing her spouse.
The later view (Abu Yusuf & Muhammad) prohibits zakat absolutely if the dower equals nisab, as a precaution.
4
Identify the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Note the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa (allows zakat absolutely for the dower case) and the two (disallow if nisab and wealthy). The mufta bihi is the precautionary view of the two.
The fatwa follows the two due to precaution, as stated in al-Baraziyya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخانية والذي له دين مؤجل على إنسان إذا احتيج إلى النفقة يجوز له أن يأخذ من الزكاة قدر كفايته إلى حلول الأجل، وإن كان الدين غير مؤجل، فإن كان من عليه الدين معسراً يجوز له أخذ الزكاة في أصح الأقاويل لأنه بمنزلة ابن السبيل، وإن كان المديون موسراً معترفاً لا يحل له أخذ الزكاة، وكذا إذا كان جاحداً وله عليه بينة عادلة، وإن لم تكن بينة عادلة لا يحل له أخذ الزكاة ما لم يرفع الأمر إلى القاضي فيحلفه، فإذا حلف بعد ذلك يحل له أخذ الزكاة ! والمراد من الدين ما يبلغ نصاباً كما لا يخفى. وفي فتح القدير : ولو دفع إلى فقيرة لها مهر دين على زوجها يبلغ نصاباً وهو موسر بحيث لو طلبت أعطاها لا يجوز، وإن كان بحيث لا يعطى لو طلبت جاز ا هـ. وهو مقيد لعموم ما في الخانية : والمراد من المهر ما تعورف تعجيله لأن ما تعورف تأجيله فهو دين مؤجل لا يمنع أخذ الزكاة ويكون في الأول عدم إعطائه بمنزلة إعساره، ويفرق بينه وبين سائر الديون بأن رفع الزوج للقاضي مما لا ينبغي للمرأة بخلاف غيره. لكن في البرازية : وإن كان موسراً والمعجل قدر النصاب لا يجوز عندهما وبه يفتى للاحتياط، وعند الإمام يجوز مطلقاً وسيأتي بيان النصب الثلاثة آخر الباب إن شاء الله تعالى.
And in al-Khaniyya: One who has a deferred debt owed to him by someone, if he needs spending [money], it is permissible for him to take from zakat an amount sufficient for his maintenance until the debt becomes due. If the debt is not deferred (i.e., immediate), if the debtor is insolvent, it is permissible for him to take zakat in the most correct of opinions, because he is like a wayfarer (ibn al-sabil). If the debtor is wealthy and admits the debt, it is not permissible for him to take zakat. Similarly, if the debtor denies the debt and the creditor has just witnesses, [he may take]. If he does not have just witnesses, it is not permissible for him to take zakat unless he brings the matter to the judge and then the debtor swears; if he swears, after that it becomes permissible for him to take zakat. And what is meant by debt is that it reaches the nisab, as is not hidden. In Fath al-Qadir: If one gives to a poor woman who has a deferred dower (mahr) owed by her husband that reaches the nisab, and he is wealthy such that if she asked he would give it, it is not permissible. If it is such that he would not give if asked, it is permissible – end quote. And this qualifies the general statement in al-Khaniyya. And what is meant by mahr is what is customarily paid promptly, because what is customarily deferred is a deferred debt that does not prevent taking zakat. In the first case, his not giving is like his insolvency. There is a distinction between this and other debts because a woman raising a matter against her husband before a judge is not appropriate, unlike others. However, in al-Baraziyya: If he is wealthy and the prompt [mahr] is of nisab amount, it is not permissible according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to this fatwa is given for precaution. According to Imam (Abu Hanifa), it is absolutely permissible. And the explanation of the three nisabs will come at the end of the chapter, God willing.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage addresses when a person who is owed a debt may receive zakat. The key distinction is between a deferred debt (due later) and an immediate debt. For a deferred debt, if the creditor needs funds for basic maintenance, he may take zakat up to his need until the debt becomes due, because his actual wealth is not accessible now. For an immediate debt, if the debtor is insolvent, the creditor may take zakat because he is like a traveler without means – his money is tied up. But if the debtor is wealthy and admits the debt, or denies but the creditor has just witnesses, the creditor cannot take zakat because he can recover the debt. If the debtor denies and the creditor lacks witnesses, he can take zakat only after the debtor swears an oath before a judge, denying the debt. The passage also discusses a special case: a woman whose husband owes her prompt dower (mahr) that equals the nisab. If the husband is wealthy and would give if asked, she cannot take zakat; if he would not give (even though wealthy), she may take zakat, because her difficulty in suing him makes the debt effectively unrecoverable. However, the later view in al-Baraziyya (the two: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) holds that if the husband is wealthy and the prompt dower equals nisab, she cannot take zakat at all, as a matter of precaution. Imam Abu Hanifa allows it absolutely. The fatwa today is on the cautious view of the two.

Key Terms
دين مؤجل (dayn mu'ajjal): A debt that is due at a future date; it does not prevent the creditor from taking zakat for immediate needs.
ابن السبيل (ibn al-sabil): Literally 'son of the road', a wayfarer or traveler cut off from resources; the insolvent debtor is analogized to this category.
المهر (al-mahr): Dower or bridewealth given by the husband to the wife, part of marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it permissible for a woman whose husband owes her a prompt dower (mahr) of nisab amount to take zakat?
A) Always, regardless of the husband's wealth
B) Only if the husband is insolvent
C) If the husband is wealthy but would not give if asked
D) Never

Key Takeaway
A creditor's eligibility for zakat depends on whether the debt is practically recoverable; deferred debts and insolvent debtors allow zakat, while wealthy admitting debtors do not; for dower, the precautionary fatwa prohibits zakat if the husband is wealthy and the dower is nisab.

The Zakat Collector's Entitlement and Its Limits
Ruling on the zakat collector's compensation and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions and maximum limits of the zakat collector’s entitlement from the zakat fund according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The zakat collector may take only a moderate wage, and at most half the zakat if his needs exhaust the fund.

This passage clarifies the compensation of the 'amil (zakat collector), a distinct category among the eight recipients of zakat. It explains that the collector is entitled to a moderate amount for himself and his assistants during the collection journey, but with a clear cap to ensure fairness to other recipients. Understanding these limits prevents misuse of zakat funds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actor and his entitlement
The passage defines the 'amil as including both the tithe collector (al-‘ashir) and the livestock collector (al-sa‘i). He is entitled to wages from the zakat fund for his work.
The term 'amil is broader than 'ashir.
2
Determine the amount: moderation and sufficiency
The collector is given what suffices him and his assistants in a moderate manner ('ala al-wasat) for the duration of the journey. This prohibits extravagance and stinginess.
The standard is al-wasat (moderation).
3
Apply the half-cap rule
If the collector's need (kifaya) would consume the entire zakat fund, he may not take more than half. This ensures other recipients receive their share.
Halving (al-tansif) is the essence of justice.
4
Consider timing and appointment
The collector may take his wages before zakat is due, but it is better to delay. The ruler must appoint a collector who is satisfied with moderation.
Hastening is permissible but discouraged.
5
Recognize the condition of remaining wealth
The entitlement lasts as long as the zakat wealth remains; if the fund is exhausted, the collector's right ceases.
Condition: bagha' al-mal (the wealth remains).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والعامل) تقدم تفسيره في باب العاشر وعبر بالعامل دون العاشر ليشمل الساعي أيضاً، وقدمنا الفرق بينهما فيعطى ما يكفيه وأعوانه بالوسط مدة ذهابهم وإيابهم ما دام المال باقياً إلا إذا استغرقت كفايته الزكاة فلا يزاد على النصف لأن التنصيف عين الإنصاف قيدنا بالوسط لأنه لا يجوز له أن يتبع شهوته في المأكل والمشرب والملبس لأنها حرام لكونها إسرافاً محضاً، وعلى الإمام أن يبعث من يرضى بالوسط من غير إسراف ولا تقتير. كذا في غاية البيان، وفي البزازية المصدق إذا أخذ عمالته قبل الوجوب أو القاضي استوفي رزقه قبل المدة جاز، والأفضل عدم التعجيل لاحتمال أن لا يعيش إلى المدة ا هـ. وقيدنا ببقاء المال
His saying: (And the worker) – its explanation has preceded in the Chapter of the Tithe Collector. He expressed 'worker' (al-‘amil) instead of 'tithe collector' (al-‘ashir) to include the collector (al-sa‘i) as well, and we have explained the difference between them. He is given what suffices him and his assistants in a moderate manner for the duration of their going and returning as long as the wealth remains. Except if his need consumes the entire zakat, then he is not given more than half, because half is the essence of justice. We restricted it with 'moderate' because it is not permissible for him to follow his desire in food, drink, and clothing, as that is forbidden due to being pure extravagance. It is incumbent upon the Imam (ruler) to send one who is satisfied with moderation without extravagance or stinginess. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. And in al-Bazzaziyya: If the assessor (musaddiq) takes his wages before the zakat becomes obligatory, or the judge takes his salary before the period, it is permissible, but it is better not to hasten because of the possibility that he may not live until the period. End quote. And we restricted it with the condition that the wealth remains.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage explains the category of the 'amil (zakat collector or worker) among the eight recipients. The author clarifies that the term 'amil includes both the 'ashir (tithe collector) and the sa'i (the one who collects zakat from livestock), as previously distinguished. The collector is entitled to a moderate amount sufficient for himself and his assistants for the duration of the collection journey, as long as there is zakat wealth. However, if his need would consume the entire zakat fund, he should not be given more than half of the zakat, because half is fair to other recipients. The condition of 'moderation' means he cannot be extravagant; he is to take only what is necessary without waste or stinginess. The Imam should appoint someone who is content with a moderate lifestyle. Additionally, a collector may take his wages before the zakat is due, but it is better to wait due to uncertainty.

Key Terms
العامل (al-‘amil): The person appointed by the ruler to collect zakat; includes the tithe collector (al-‘ashir) and the one who collects zakat from livestock (al-sa‘i).
الوسط (al-wasat): Moderation; a standard of sufficiency without extravagance or parsimony.
التنصيف (al-tansif): Halving; the principle that the ‘amil should not take more than half the zakat if his need consumes the whole fund.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The entire zakat
B) Half of the zakat
C) Enough for his journey only
D) Nothing, since he must work for free

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts the zakat collector's wage to a moderate amount, capped at half the fund if his need exhausts it, to ensure justice among recipients.

Zakat and Bequest: Distribution to a Single Category
Compares zakat and bequest rulings using talil reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi rulings on giving zakat versus a bequest to a single category of recipients and explain the legal rationale (illah) for each.

Core Idea
Zakat can go to one category; a bequest must follow the testator's literal words.

This lesson examines a key contrast in Hanafi fiqh: why it is permissible to disburse all your zakat to a single category of the eight recipient types, but if someone bequeaths a portion of their wealth to multiple categories, you cannot give it all to just one. The difference lies in the purpose of each obligation. Zakat is to fulfill urgent need, so any category that receives it satisfies that need. A bequest, however, reflects the testator’s unspoken intentions, which may be many; therefore, his words must be followed exactly. We will unpack the reasoning from the source text in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts and their rulings
Identify that the passage discusses: (1) giving zakat to a single category – permissible; (2) executing a bequest (wasiyyah) to a single category when the testator named multiple categories – not permissible according to the correct view.
2
Locate the illah (cause) for each
The text states that zakat is legislated to fulfill the pressing need of the poor, and that need is met by giving to one category. A bequest, however, is not based on need – it is even permissible for a rich person to receive a bequest – and the testator may have many unknown objectives.
This is a talil (causal reasoning) argument.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on bequest
The passage reports a minority view (qīl yajūz) that it is permissible to give a bequest to one category. But the correct (ṣaḥīḥ) view, from al-Badā’i‘ and al-Muḥīṭ, is that it is not permissible. The tarjīḥ relies on the principle that a bequest is executed literally.
4
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Take a concrete example: A man bequeaths one-third of his estate to the seven categories (the eight zakat categories minus one, or any set of categories). The executor must distribute among all seven; giving to only one is invalid. If the executor gave to one, the bequest would be void for the other six.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فعلى الصحيح لفلان ثلث الثلث، وعلى غيره نصف الثلث، وإنما جاز صرف الزكاة إلى صنف واحد لمعنى لا يوجد في الوصية وهو دفع الحاجة وذا يحصل بالصرف إلى صنف واحد والوصية ما شرعت لدفع حاجة الموصى له فإنها تجوز للغني أيضاً، وقد يكون للموصى أغراض كثيرة لا يوقف عليها فلا يمكن تعليل نص كلامه فيجري على ظاهر لفظه من غير اعتبار المعنى. كذا في البدائع ولهذا لو أوصى بثلث ماله للأصناف السبعة فصرف إلى صنف واحد لا يجوز، وقيل يجوز . كذا في المحيط.
According to the correct view, one person gets a third of the third, and another gets half of the third. It is permissible to disburse zakat to a single category due to a meaning not found in a bequest, which is the fulfillment of need; this is achieved by disbursement to one category. A bequest is not legislated to fulfill the need of the legatee, for it is permissible for the rich as well. And the testator may have many objectives that cannot be known, so it is not possible to interpret his wording by considering the meaning; thus it is taken according to the apparent wording without considering the meaning. Thus in al-Bada'i. For this reason, if one bequeaths one-third of his wealth to the seven categories, and then distributes it to a single category, it is not permissible, and it is said it is permissible. Thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the permissibility of giving zakat to one category of recipients, contrasted with the requirements for a bequest (wasiyyah). The commentator explains that zakat is given to meet the immediate need of the poor, and that need can be fulfilled by giving to one category. In contrast, a bequest is not based on need—it is permissible for a rich person to receive a bequest—and the testator may have multiple intentions that cannot be ascertained. Therefore, the wording of the bequest must be followed literally, without interpreting based on supposed need. Hence, if someone bequeaths one-third of his wealth to the seven categories (the zakat recipients), he must distribute to all seven; giving to just one category is invalid according to the correct view, though there is an opinion that it is permissible. The commentator cites al-Bada'i and al-Muhit.

Key Terms
صنف واحد (sinf wahid): One category of the eight zakat recipients mentioned in Quran 9:60.
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest made by a testator, which must be executed according to its literal wording.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it permissible to give zakat to a single category but not to distribute a bequest to only one category?
A) Because zakat is fard and bequest is sunnah.
B) Because zakat is for fulfilling need, which is achieved by one category, whereas a bequest serves multiple unknown intentions of the testator.
C) Because zakat recipients are poorer than bequest recipients.
D) Because bequest is only for relatives.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, zakat may be given to one category because its purpose is fulfilling need, while a bequest must follow the testator's literal wording due to unknown intentions.

Ruling on a Creditor Taking Zakat
Conditions for a creditor taking zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a creditor may take zakat and apply the analogy of ibn al-sabil to determine permissibility.

Core Idea
A creditor in need may take zakat if the debtor is insolvent, by analogy to the stranded traveler.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details the nuanced rulings on creditors taking zakat. It distinguishes between deferred and immediate debts, and considers the debtor's solvency and acknowledgment. The key analogy is to the Quranic category of ibn al-sabil (stranded traveler). We will walk through the conditions and examine an intra-Hanafi difference on the case of a woman's unpaid dower.

Guided Path
1
Identify the creditor's situation
Determine whether the debt is deferred (mu'ajjal) or immediate (hal), as the ruling differs.
2
Analyze the qiyas to ibn al-sabil
For an immediate debt with an insolvent debtor, the creditor is like a stranded traveler: both have wealth that is inaccessible. This is an istihsan based on need.
3
Apply the conditions for immediate debt
If the debtor is solvent and acknowledges, the creditor cannot take zakat. If the debtor denies, the creditor needs just witnesses; otherwise, must go to court for an oath.
4
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr
Imam Abu Hanifa permits a woman with unpaid mahr to take zakat absolutely, but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad restrict it if the husband is solvent and would pay. The fatwa is with the latter for precaution.
The dispute hinges on whether the wife's ability to demand payment makes her wealth accessible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخانية والذي له دين مؤجل على إنسان إذا احتيج إلى النفقة يجوز له أن يأخذ من الزكاة قدر كفايته إلى حلول الأجل، وإن كان الدين غير مؤجل، فإن كان من عليه الدين معسراً يجوز له أخذ الزكاة في أصح الأقاويل لأنه بمنزلة ابن السبيل، وإن كان المديون موسراً معترفاً لا يحل له أخذ الزكاة، وكذا إذا كان جاحداً وله عليه بينة عادلة، وإن لم تكن بينة عادلة لا يحل له أخذ الزكاة ما لم يرفع الأمر إلى القاضي فيحلفه، فإذا حلف بعد ذلك يحل له أخذ الزكاة ! والمراد من الدين ما يبلغ نصاباً كما لا يخفى. وفي فتح القدير : ولو دفع إلى فقيرة لها مهر دين على زوجها يبلغ نصاباً وهو موسر بحيث لو طلبت أعطاها لا يجوز، وإن كان بحيث لا يعطى لو طلبت جاز ا هـ. وهو مقيد لعموم ما في الخانية : والمراد من المهر ما تعورف تعجيله لأن ما تعورف تأجيله فهو دين مؤجل لا يمنع أخذ الزكاة ويكون في الأول عدم إعطائه بمنزلة إعساره، ويفرق بينه وبين سائر الديون بأن رفع الزوج للقاضي مما لا ينبغي للمرأة بخلاف غيره. لكن في البرازية : وإن كان موسراً والمعجل قدر النصاب لا يجوز عندهما وبه يفتى للاحتياط، وعند الإمام يجوز مطلقاً وسيأتي بيان النصب الثلاثة آخر الباب إن شاء الله تعالى. : هـ. قوله : (وسيأتي بيان النصب الخ) أي عند شرح قوله
And in al-Khaniyya: He who has a deferred debt on someone, if he needs maintenance, it is permissible for him to take from zakat up to his sufficiency until the term matures. If the debt is not deferred, then if the debtor is insolvent, it is permissible for him to take zakat in the most correct narrations, because he is like a stranded traveler. If the debtor is solvent and acknowledges, it is not permissible for him to take zakat. Similarly, if he denies and he has just witnesses against him, and if he does not have just witnesses, it is not permissible for him to take zakat unless he takes the matter to the judge and [the debtor] takes an oath; then if he takes an oath after that, it becomes permissible for him to take zakat. The intent by 'debt' is that it reaches the threshold of nisab, as is obvious. And in Fath al-Qadir: If one gives to a poor woman who has a dower debt on her husband reaching nisab while he is solvent such that if she demanded he would give it, it is not permissible. If he would not give if demanded, it is permissible. This qualifies the generality of what is in al-Khaniyya. And the intent by 'dower' is what is customarily given immediately, for what is customarily deferred is a deferred debt that does not prevent taking zakat. And in the first case, his not giving is akin to his insolvency. And there is a distinction between this and other debts in that taking the husband to the judge is not befitting of the woman, unlike others. However, in al-Birzaliyya: If he is solvent and the immediate portion reaches nisab, it is not permissible according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and this is the fatwa for precaution, while according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) it is absolutely permissible. And soon the explanation of the three nusub will come at the end of the chapter, God willing. This ends. He said: 'And soon the explanation of the nusub will come'—i.e., when explaining his statement.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage provides detailed rulings on when a person who is owed a debt may take zakat. The key distinction is whether the debt is deferred or immediate. For a deferred debt, if the creditor is in need, he may take zakat up to his needs until the debt is due. For an immediate debt, the debtor's financial status and acknowledgment matter. If the debtor is insolvent, the creditor is like a stranded traveler (ibn al-sabil) and may take zakat. If the debtor is solvent and acknowledges the debt, the creditor cannot take zakat. If the debtor denies the debt, the creditor needs just witnesses; otherwise, he must go to court and have the debtor swear an oath. A special case is a woman with an unpaid dower (mahr): if the husband is solvent and would pay if asked, she cannot take zakat; if he would not pay, she can, because his refusal is like insolvency. There is an intra-Hanafi difference: Imam Abu Hanifa permits absolutely, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad prohibit if the husband is solvent and the immediate portion reaches nisab, and the fatwa is given for precaution (ihtiyat). The passage also notes that the term 'debt' here means a sum that reaches nisab.

Key Terms
دين مؤجل (dayn mu'ajjal): A debt with a fixed future term for payment.
ابن السبيل (ibn al-sabil): A stranded traveler who is cut off from his wealth; a Quranic zakat recipient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) If the debtor is solvent and acknowledges the debt.
B) If the debtor is insolvent.
C) If the debt is less than nisab.
D) If the creditor is rich.

Key Takeaway
A creditor in need may take zakat when the debt is deferred or the debtor is insolvent, by analogy to ibn al-sabil.

Compensation of the Zakat Collector (al-'Amiil)
Ruling with proof on 'amiil compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the amount and conditions of the 'amiil's compensation and identify the ruling on early payment.

Core Idea
The 'amiil's compensation is moderate and limited to half if needed; early payment is permissible but discouraged.

In this section, we learn about the compensation given to the zakat collector ('amiil) for his work. The text details that he is to be given a moderate amount for himself and his helpers, with a maximum of half the zakat if his needs consume the entire fund. It also discusses whether he can take payment before the zakat is due, and includes a note about denied debts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and its ruling
The subject is the compensation of the 'amiil. The ruling is that he is given moderate sufficiency (al-wasat) as long as the money lasts.
2
List the key conditions
Condition: moderation in food, drink, and clothing; no extravagance. Limit: if his sufficiency consumes the zakat, he is not given more than half.
Half is based on fairness (al-insaf).
3
Analyze the early payment ruling
From al-Birzaliyya: it is permissible for the 'amiil to take his commission before the zakat is due, but it is better not to hasten due to the risk of death.
Similar ruling applies to a judge taking salary before term.
4
Examine the denied debt note
The text inserts a note: a denied debt does not count as nisab, and not every judge is just; litigation is difficult. This relates to the 'amiil's collection process.
This is from al-Nahr and al-Sarakhsi.
5
Summarize the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position: compensation is moderate and permissible; early payment is permissible but discouraged.
Source: Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Birzaliyya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والعامل) تقدم تفسيره في باب العاشر وعبر بالعامل دون العاشر ليشمل الساعي أيضاً، وقدمنا الفرق بينهما فيعطى ما يكفيه وأعوانه بالوسط مدة ذهابهم وإيابهم ما دام المال باقياً إلا إذا استغرقت كفايته الزكاة فلا يزاد على النصف لأن التنصيف عين الإنصاف قيدنا بالوسط لأنه لا يجوز له أن يتبع شهوته في المأكل والمشرب والملبس لأنها حرام لكونها إسرافاً محضاً، وعلى الإمام أن يبعث من يرضى بالوسط من غير إسراف ولا تقتير. كذا في غاية البيان، وفي البزازية المصدق إذا أخذ عمالته قبل الوجوب أو القاضي استوفي رزقه قبل المدة جاز، والأفضل عدم التعجيل لاحتمال أن لا يعيش إلى المدة ا هـ. وقيدنا ببقاء المال قوله : (وكذا إذا كان جاحداً (الخ قال في النهر : بقي أنه في الأصل لم يجعل الدين المجحود نصاباً ولم يفصل بين ما إذا كان له بينة عادلة أو لا. قال السرخسي : والصحيح جواب الكتاب إذ ليس كل قاض يعدل ولا كل بينة تقبل والجثو بين يدي القاضي ذل وكل أحد لا يختار ذلك، وينبغي أن يعول على هذا كما في عقد الفرائد ا هـ 
كتاب الزكاة باب المصرف ٤٢١ ومنقطع الغزاة وابن السبيل فيدفع إلى كلهم أو إلى صنف لا إلى ذمي وصح غيرها وبناء لأنه لو أخذ الصدقة وضاعت في يده بطلت عمالته ولا يعطى من بيت المال شيئاً. كذا في الأجناس عن الزيادات وما يأخذه العامل صدقة فلا تحل العمالة لهاشمي لشرفه كما سيأتي، وإنما حلت للغني مع حرمة الصدقة عليه لأنه فرغ نفسه لهذا العمل فيحتاج إلى الكفاية والغنى لا يمنع من تناولها عند الحاجة كابن السبيل. كذا في البدائع. والتحقيق أن فيه شبهاً بالأجرة وشبهاً بالصدقة فللأول يحل للغني ولا يعطى لو هلك المال أو أداها صاحب المال إلى الإمام، وللثاني لا يحل للهاشمي. ويسقط الواجب عن أرباب الأموال لو هلك المال في يده لأن يده كيد الإمام وهو نائب عن الفقراء ولا تكون مقدرة. وفي النهاية: رجل من بني هاشم استعمل على الصدقة فأجري له منها رزق فإنه لا ينبغي له أن يأخذ من ذلك، وإن عمل فيها ورزق من غيرها فلا بأس بذلك اهـ. وهو يفيد صحة توليته وأن أخذه منها مكروه لا حرام. ومن أحكام العامل ما ذكره في البزازية أن العامل إذا ترك الخراج على المزارع بدون علم السلطان يحل له لو مصرفاً كالسلطان إذا ترك الخراج له
His saying: (and the 'amiil) – his explanation preceded in the chapter of the 'aashir. He used the term 'amiil rather than 'aashir to include the sa'i as well. We have previously mentioned the difference between them. He is given what suffices him and his helpers at a moderate level during the period of their going and returning as long as the money remains. Except if his sufficiency consumes the zakat, then it is not increased beyond half, because half is precisely fairness. We restricted moderation because it is not permissible for him to follow his desires in food, drink, and clothing, for that is haram due to being pure waste. It is upon the imam to send someone who accepts moderation without waste or stinginess. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. And in al-Birzaliyya: the collector (musaddiq) if he takes his commission before obligation, or the judge takes his salary before the term, it is permissible, but it is better not to hasten due to the possibility that he may not live until the term. And we restricted to the survival of the wealth. His saying: (and also if he denies...) – he said in al-Nahr: remains that in the original work, he did not make the denied debt a nisab and did not distinguish between whether he has just witnesses or not. Al-Sarakhsi said: the correct answer of the book is that not every judge is just, nor is every witness accepted, and standing before the judge is humiliation, and not everyone chooses that, and one should rely on this, as in 'Uqd al-Fara'id. Book of Zakat, Chapter of Expenditure. page 421. And the cut-off ones (munqati') and the stranded traveler (ibn al-sabil): it is given to all of them or to one category, but not to a dhimmī. It is valid for others and based on... because if he takes the charity and it is lost in his hand, his commission becomes void and he is not given anything from the treasury. Thus in al-Ajnas from al-Ziyadat. And what the 'amiil takes is sadaqah (charity), so the post of 'amiil is not permissible for a Hashimi due to his nobility, as will come. But it is permissible for the wealthy despite the prohibition of sadaqah on him because he has devoted himself to this work, so he needs sufficiency, and wealth does not prevent taking it when in need, like ibn al-sabil. Thus in al-Bada'i. The investigation is that it resembles both ajr (wage) and sadaqah. For the first, it is permissible for the wealthy, and he is not given if the wealth perishes or the owner pays it to the imam. For the second, it is not permissible for the Hashimi. And the obligation is dropped from the owners if the wealth perishes in his hand, because his hand is like the imam's hand, and he is a deputy for the poor, and it is not determined. In al-Nihaya: a man from Banu Hashim was employed over the charity and a stipend was assigned to him from it; it is not proper for him to take from that if he works in it, but if he is given a stipend from elsewhere, there is no harm. This indicates the validity of his appointment and that his taking from it is makruh (disliked), not haram. From the rulings of the 'amiil is what is mentioned in al-Birzaliyya: if the 'amiil abandons the kharaj on the farmer without the knowledge of the sultan, it is permissible for him if he is a disburser? Like the sultan if he abandons the kharaj for him.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage deals with the zakat collector ('amiil). The commentator explains that the 'amiil is given moderate compensation (al-wasat) for himself and his helpers during their journey to collect zakat, as long as the zakat money remains. If his entire sufficiency consumes the zakat, he is limited to half. He may not indulge in luxury. It is also discussed whether he can take payment before the zakat is due; it is permissible but discouraged to hasten. The commentary then includes a note from al-Nahr about denied debts and the difficulty of taking a debtor to court. Returning to the 'amiil, the text explains that what he takes is sadaqah, and therefore a Hashimi cannot serve as 'amiil because sadaqah is prohibited for Hashimis. However, a wealthy non-Hashimi can serve because he needs the compensation. The 'amiil's payment has a dual nature: it is like a wage (ajr) in that it is permissible for the wealthy, and like sadaqah in that it is prohibited for Hashimis. The passage also covers that if the zakat is lost in the 'amiil's hand, the obligation of the owners is dropped, as his hand is like the imam's. A Hashimi can be appointed but should not take from the zakat; he should be paid from other sources, making the taking from zakat makruh (disliked) but not haram. Finally, a ruling about the 'amiil may forgo kharaj from farmers without the sultan's knowledge, which may be permissible if he is acting as a disburser.

Key Terms
العامل (al-'amiil): The zakat collector appointed by the imam, including the 'aashir and sa'i.
الوسط (al-wasat): Moderation; the middle path without extravagance or stinginess.

Key Terms from Source Passage

When does the half-limit on the 'amiil's compensation apply?
A) Always, regardless of the amount of zakat
B) Only when the 'amiil's moderate needs are greater than the zakat collected
C) Only when the 'amiil is a Hashimi
D) When the zakat money is abundant

Key Takeaway
The 'amiil's compensation is moderate and limited to half if his needs consume the zakat; early payment is permissible but discouraged.

Can a Hashimi Be a Zakat Collector?
Ruling with proof on Hashimi eligibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the 'amiil's compensation is prohibited for Hashimi and distinguish between makruh and haram in this context.

Core Idea
The 'amiil's pay resembles both wage and sadaqah, making it halal for wealthy non-Hashimi but prohibited for Hashimi; appointment is valid but taking from zakat is makruh.

This lesson addresses the eligibility of a Hashimi (descendant of Hashim) to serve as zakat collector. The text explains that what the 'amiil takes is sadaqah, and sadaqah is haram for the Hashimi. However, it also clarifies that the payment has a dual nature—similar to both wages and charity—and a Hashimi can be appointed if paid from other sources. Taking from zakat is considered makruh (disliked) but not haram.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule: sadaqah is haram for Hashimi
The text opens with 'وما يأخذه العامل صدقة فلا تحل العمالة لهاشمي' – what the 'amiil takes is sadaqah, so the post is not halal for a Hashimi.
Based on the established prohibition of sadaqah on the Prophet's family.
2
Analyze the dual nature of the 'amiil's payment
The payment has two aspects: it resembles ajr (wage) because it is for work, and sadaqah because it comes from zakat. This duality leads to different rulings.
From al-Bada'i: 'fihi shubhatun bi'l-ajrati wa shubhatun bi's-sadaqati'.
3
Examine the exception for a wealthy 'amiil
A wealthy non-Hashimi can take because he is in need due to his work; wealth does not prevent taking when in need (like ibn al-sabil).
The text says: 'inna hulla lil-ghani ma'a hurmati's-sadaqati 'alayhi'.
4
Find the ruling on Hashimi appointment and payment
From al-Nihaya: a Hashimi can be appointed, but should not take from zakat; if he does, it is makruh not haram. Taking from other sources is fine.
The text: 'wa huwa yufidu sahha tawliyatihi wa anna akhudha minha makruhun la haramun'.
5
Consider the consequence if wealth perishes
If the zakat is lost in the 'amiil's hand, the obligation drops from the owners, as his hand is like the imam's and he is a deputy for the poor.
This applies regardless of Hashimi status.

The Zakat Collector's Compensation and the Hashimi Exception
Explanation of collector's compensation and Hashimi exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the zakat collector's payment is permissible for a wealthy collector but prohibited for a Hashimi, and state the ruling if funds are lost.

Core Idea
The collector's payment resembles both a wage and sadaqah — permissibility for the rich, prohibition for the Hashimi.

The zakat collector (al-‘āmil) is a deputy of the Imam, entitled to compensation for his work. This passage explores the dual nature of that compensation: it resembles a wage (ujrah) and also sadaqah. This dual resemblance explains why a wealthy collector may take it (like a wage) and why a Hashimi descendant may not (like sadaqah). Understanding this reasoning is key to applying the rule correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the collector taking his compensation from the zakat funds. Determine the hukm for a rich collector (permissible) and for a Hashimi collector (makruh tahrimi).
The text states: 'What the collector takes is sadaqah, so the employment is not permissible for a Hashimi' and 'it became permissible for the rich despite the prohibition of sadaqah upon him'.
2
Locate the dalil and its type
The proof is not a direct Quran or hadith but a talil (reasoning) based on the dual resemblance (shabah) of the payment to wage and sadaqah.
The author says: 'The verification is that it has a resemblance to a wage and a resemblance to sadaqah.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each resemblance yields a ruling. For the rich: because it resembles a wage, the general prohibition of sadaqah for the rich is lifted due to need (the collector devotes his time). For the Hashimi: because it resembles sadaqah, the prohibition applies to them as they cannot take sadaqah.
The text adds: 'he has devoted himself to this work, so he needs sufficiency, and wealth does not prevent him from taking it when there is need, like the wayfarer.'
4
Note the ikhtilaf and the Hashimi exception
The Hashimi exception is a point of ikhtilaf. The Hanafi position: appointment is valid, but taking from zakat funds is makruh tahrimi. If paid from other sources, it is permissible.
Al-Nihayah: 'it indicates the validity of his appointment and that his taking from it is makruh, not haram.'
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that a Hashimi should not take from zakat funds, but may be appointed and paid from non-zakat sources.
The text does not mention a tarjih authority, but the ruling from al-Nihayah is considered reliable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة باب المصرف ومنقطع الغزاة وابن السبيل فيدفع إلى كلهم أو إلى صنف لا إلى ذمي وصح غيرها وبناء لأنه لو أخذ الصدقة وضاعت في يده بطلت عمالته ولا يعطى من بيت المال شيئاً. كذا في الأجناس عن الزيادات وما يأخذه العامل صدقة فلا تحل العمالة لهاشمي لشرفه كما سيأتي، وإنما حلت للغني مع حرمة الصدقة عليه لأنه فرغ نفسه لهذا العمل فيحتاج إلى الكفاية والغنى لا يمنع من تناولها عند الحاجة كابن السبيل. كذا في البدائع. والتحقيق أن فيه شبهاً بالأجرة وشبهاً بالصدقة فللأول يحل للغني ولا يعطى لو هلك المال أو أداها صاحب المال إلى الإمام، وللثاني لا يحل للهاشمي. ويسقط الواجب عن أرباب الأموال لو هلك المال في يده لأن يده كيد الإمام وهو نائب عن الفقراء ولا تكون مقدرة. وفي النهاية: رجل من بني هاشم استعمل على الصدقة فأجري له منها رزق فإنه لا ينبغي له أن يأخذ من ذلك، وإن عمل فيها ورزق من غيرها فلا بأس بذلك اهـ. وهو يفيد صحة توليته وأن أخذه منها مكروه لا حرام. ومن أحكام العامل ما ذكره في البزازية أن العامل إذا ترك الخراج على المزارع بدون علم السلطان يحل له لو مصرفاً كالسلطان إذا ترك الخراج له
Book of Zakat, Chapter of Recipients: And those cut off from their resources for the cause of Allah and the wayfarer: so it is given to all of them or to one category, not to a dhimmi. And other than it is valid, and it is based on the fact that if he took the sadaqah and it was lost in his hand, his employment is void, and he is not given anything from the public treasury. Likewise in al-Ajnas from al-Ziyadat. And what the collector takes is sadaqah, so the employment is not permissible for a Hashimi due to his nobility, as will come. Rather, it became permissible for the rich despite the prohibition of sadaqah upon him because he has devoted himself to this work, so he needs sufficiency, and wealth does not prevent him from taking it when there is need, like the wayfarer. Likewise in al-Bada'i'. And the verification is that it has a resemblance to a wage and a resemblance to sadaqah. For the first, it is permissible for the rich, and he is not given if the wealth is lost or if the owner of the wealth gives it to the Imam. For the second, it is not permissible for the Hashimi. And the obligation falls from the owners of wealth if the wealth is lost in his hand, because his hand is like the hand of the Imam, and he is a deputy for the poor, and he is not considered reliable. And in al-Nihayah: A man from Banu Hashim was appointed over sadaqah, and a stipend from it was arranged for him: he should not take any of that, and if he works in it and is given provision from other than it, there is no harm in that. It indicates the validity of his appointment and that his taking from it is makruh, not haram. And from the rulings of the collector is what al-Bazzaziyyah mentioned: that if the collector leaves the kharaj upon the farmer without the knowledge of the sultan, it is permissible for him as a dispensation, like the sultan when he leaves the kharaj for him.
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling of the zakat collector (al-‘āmil). The author discusses the nature of his compensation, which resembles both a wage (ujrah) and a charity (ṣadaqah). Due to the resemblance to wage, it is permissible for a rich collector to receive it, as he has devoted his time to the work. If the collected wealth is lost without negligence, the obligation of zakat is discharged from the donors because the collector is a deputy of the Imam. However, due to the resemblance to charity, it is not permissible for a Hashimi (descendant of the Prophet) to take it, as they are forbidden from accepting sadaqah. The text further clarifies that a Hashimi may be appointed as a collector, but he should not take from the zakat funds; he may be paid from other sources. This is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), not haram. The passage also mentions a ruling from al-Bazzaziyyah regarding the collector's discretion in collecting kharaj.

Key Terms
العامل (al-‘āmil): The official collector appointed by the Imam to collect zakat from the wealthy and distribute it to the deserving.
هاشمي (Hāshimī): A descendant of Banu Hashim, the clan of the Prophet Muhammad, who are prohibited from receiving sadaqah.
الأجرة (al-ujrah): Wage paid for work or service.
شبه (shabah): Resemblance; a concept used to analogize a mixed case to two categories.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling for a Hashimi collector who takes his compensation from the zakat funds?
A) Haram
B) Makruh tahrimi
C) Makruh tanzihi
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The collector's payment has a dual resemblance (shabah) to wage and sadaqah, making it permissible for the rich but not for Hashimis, who are honored by prohibition from sadaqah.

Zakat for the Mukatab: Ownership and Conditions
Discussion of whether the mukatab owns the zakat given to him, with proofs from Quran and tafsir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ownership of zakat given to a mukatab, identify the exception for Hashimi mukatab, and apply the principle of tamlik in zakat distribution.

Core Idea
A mukatab owns the zakat given to him because it is tamlik, except for a Hashimi mukatab due to the master’s shadow ownership.

Zakat can be given to help a mukatab (a slave under contract of emancipation) free himself. But does the mukatab actually own the money, or is it strictly for his master? This lesson examines the Quranic phrase 'fi al-riqab' and the Hanafi ruling that giving zakat to a mukatab is a transfer of ownership (tamlik), with one important exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its Quranic basis
The passage discusses giving zakat to a mukatab under the category 'fi al-riqab' (in the necks) from Quran 2:177. Note that the preposition 'fi' (in) instead of 'lam' (for) is used.
This grammatical choice is key to the dispute.
2
Analyze the grammatical argument against ownership
Some tafsirs (e.g., al-Baydawi, al-Tibi) argue that 'fi' indicates the money is for the purpose of emancipation, not for personal ownership. They say the four categories after the first four in the verse do not become owners.
They claim the mukatab does not own the zakat.
3
Apply the Hanafi position from al-Bada'i'
Al-Bada'i' states that giving to the mukatab is tamlik (making owner), which implies ownership falls to the mukatab. This is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.
Tamlik overrides the grammatical argument.
4
Recognize the exception: Hashimi mukatab
It is not permissible for a Hashimi mukatab to receive zakat because ownership ultimately goes to the master in one respect, and the prohibition of sadaqah for Hashimis applies.
This is based on al-Muhit.
5
Apply the same principle to other categories
If a poor recipient becomes rich, or a wayfarer reaches home, the zakat already given is not returned, similarly if the mukatab becomes unable, the master may take what was given.
Ownership is established at the time of giving.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والمكاتب) أي يعان المكاتب في فك رقبته وهو المراد بقوله تعالى ﴿وفي الرقاب﴾ [البقرة: ١٧٧] هو منقول عن الحسن البصري وغيره في تفسير الطبري وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان مولاه فقيراً أو غنياً. وهل ما يدفع للمكاتب منها يكون ملكاً له أو لا؟ فالذي في بعض التفاسير أنه لا يملك. قال القاضي البيضاوي والعدول عن اللام إلى (في) للدلالة على أن الاستحقاق للجهة لا للرقاب. وقيل للإيذان بأنهم أحق بها .ا.هـ. وقال الطيبي في حاشية الكشاف : إنما عدل عن اللام إلى «في» في الأربعة الأخيرة لأن الأربعة الأولى ملاك لما عسى أن يدفع إليهم. والأربعة الأخيرة لا يملكون ما يدفع إليهم إنما يصرف المال في مصالح تتعلق بهم لأن التعدية بـ«في» مقدر بالصرف، فمال الرقاب يملكه السادة والمكاتبون لا يحصل في أيديهم شيء، والغارمون بصرف نصيبهم لأرباب الديون، وكذلك في سبيل الله تعالى وابن السبيل مندرج في سبيل الله وأفرد بالذكر تنبيهاً على خصوصية وهو مجرد عن الحرفين جميعاً أي اللام وفي وعطفه على اللام ممكن وفي أقرب ا هـ . فقد بأن الأربعة الأخيرة لا صرح يملكون شيئاً، ويستفاد منه أنهم ليس لهم صرف المال في غير الجهة التي أخذوا لأجلها. وفي البدائع : وإنما جاز دفع الزكاة إلى المكاتب لأن الدفع إليه تمليك وهو ظاهر في أن الملك يقع للمكاتب فبقية الأربعة بالطريقة الأولى لكن بقي هل لهم على هذا الصرف إلى غير الجهة. قوله : (لكن بقي الخ قال الرملي الذي يقتضيه نظر الفقيه الجواز تأمل ا هـ . قلت : بل جزم وفي المحيط : وقد قالوا إنه لا يجوز لمكاتب هاشمي لأن الملك يقع للمولى من وجه والشبهة ملحقة بالحقيقة في حقهم ا هـ . وفي شرح المجمع : وإن عجز المكاتب يحل لمولاه وإن كان غنياً، وعلى هذا الفقير إذا استغنى وابن السبيل إذا وصل إلى ماله .
His statement: (And the mukatab) i.e. the mukatab is assisted in freeing his neck, and that is intended by His statement: 'And in the necks' [2:177]. It is transmitted from al-Hasan al-Basri and others in Tafsir al-Tabari. And it is absolute, so it includes whether his master is poor or rich. And does what is given to the mukatab from it become his property or not? What is in some tafsirs is that he does not own it. Al-Qadi al-Baydawi said: The turning away from the lam to 'fi' indicates that the entitlement is for the category, not for the necks. And it is said to indicate that they are more deserving of it. Al-Tibi said in his commentary on al-Kashshaf: The lam is turned away to 'fi' in the last four because the first four are owners of what might be given to them, while the last four do not own what is given to them; rather, the money is spent on interests related to them because the transitive use with 'fi' implies spending. So the wealth of necks is owned by the masters, and the mukatabun do not get anything in their hands; the debtors spend their share on the creditors; likewise 'in the way of Allah' and the wayfarer is included in 'the way of Allah' and is mentioned separately to draw attention to its specialty. And it is free from both prepositions, i.e. lam and fi, and its conjunction with lam is possible, but with fi is closer. So it is clear that the last four do not own anything explicitly, and it is understood that they cannot spend the money on other than the purpose for which they took it. In al-Bada'i': It is permissible to give zakat to the mukatab because giving to him is a giving of ownership, which is apparent in that ownership falls to the mukatab. So the remaining four are by the primary method, but there remains whether they can spend it on other than the purpose. His statement: (But there remains... al-Ramli said: What the jurist's view requires is permissibility. I said: Rather it is decisive.) And in al-Muhit: They said: It is not permissible for a Hashimi mukatab because ownership falls to the master in one respect and the suspicion is attached to reality in their case. And in Sharh al-Majma': If the mukatab becomes unable, it is permissible for his master (to take what was given), even if he is rich. And on this, the poor person if he becomes rich, and the wayfarer if he reaches his wealth.
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on giving zakat to a mukatab (a slave who has a contract of emancipation). The author discusses the meaning of 'fi al-riqab' from the Quran (2:177). There is a difference of opinion on whether the mukatab owns the zakat given to him. Some tafsirs indicate he does not own it, because the preposition 'fi' (in) instead of 'lam' (for) suggests the money is for the purpose of emancipation, not for personal ownership. However, in al-Bada'i', it is argued that giving to the mukatab is tamlik (making owner), so he does own it. The text then notes an exception: for a Hashimi mukatab, it is not permissible because ownership goes to the master in a way, and the suspicion of impermissibility attaches to them. Additionally, if the mukatab becomes unable to pay, what was given becomes permissible for the master. The same principle applies to a poor person who later becomes rich or a wayfarer who reaches his wealth: the zakat given is no longer needed but they are not required to return it.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukātab): A slave who has entered into a contract of emancipation (kitabah) with his master, to pay a sum in installments in exchange for freedom.
تمليك (tamlīk): Making someone an owner; transferring ownership of property to another person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on giving zakat to a Hashimi mukatab?
A) It is permissible because he is needy.
B) It is not permissible because ownership ultimately goes to the master, and Hashimis are prohibited from sadaqah.
C) It is obligatory because it helps in emancipation.
D) It is recommended only if the master is poor.

Key Takeaway
A mukatab owns the zakat given to him as tamlik, with the exception of Hashimi mukatab and a caveat for the master if the mukatab becomes unable.

Zakat for the Indebted Person (al-Madyun)
Defining the indebted person and his eligibility for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for an indebted person to receive zakat and explain why giving to such a person is preferred over a poor person without debt.

Core Idea
An indebted person who lacks surplus nisab is eligible for zakat and takes priority over the poor.

Zakat is prescribed for eight categories, including the 'gharim' (one burdened with debt). This lesson clarifies who qualifies as an indebted recipient and highlights a preference in distribution. Understanding the condition of not owning surplus nisab ensures that zakat reaches those truly in need.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage discusses giving zakat to an indebted person (al-madyun). It notes that the primary text (al-Quduri) stated it absolutely, but later sources added a condition.
2
Understand the condition from al-Kafi
Al-Kafi restricts the eligibility to one who does not own surplus nisab beyond his debt. This means that after paying the debt, he would not own nisab.
The condition ensures that the debtor is genuinely needy, not just someone who has assets but also liabilities.
3
Trace the dalil – Quranic basis
The term 'gharim' in Surah At-Tawbah (9:60) is the proof. In language, it means one who has a debt and cannot repay. The Hanafi school interprets this as requiring that the person does not have surplus wealth.
The verse: '…and for the gharimin…' indicates their eligibility.
4
Recognize the author's reconciliation
The commentator explains that the author of the matn did not explicitly mention the condition because poverty is already a general condition for all zakat recipients except the collector and the wayfarer (if he has wealth in his homeland). Thus, the condition is implicit.
5
Note the preference from al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah
The text states that giving zakat to an indebted person is better (awla) than giving to a poor person without debt. This is because the debt is a pressing need.
This preference applies when both recipients are equal in other respects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والمديون) أطلقه كالقدوري وقيده في الكافي بأن لا يملك نصاباً فاضلاً. دينه لأنه المراد بالغارم في الآية وهو في اللغة من عليه دين ولا يجد قضاء كما ذكره القتبي . وإنما لم يقيده المصنف لأن الفقر شرط في الأصناف كلها إلا العامل وابن السبيل إذا كان له في وطنه مال بمنزلة الفقير . وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية والدفع إلى من عليه الدين أولى من الدفع إلى الفقير
His statement: (And the indebted) he gave it absolutely like al-Quduri, and al-Kafi restricted it by that he does not own surplus nisab above his debt, because that is intended by 'al-gharim' in the verse, and in the language it is one upon whom there is a debt and he does not find means to pay it, as al-Qutaybi mentioned. And the author did not restrict it because poverty is a condition in all categories except the collector and the wayfarer if he has wealth in his homeland, he is like the poor. And in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: Giving to one who has a debt is better than giving to a poor person.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage defines al-madyun (the indebted person) who is eligible for zakat. The author notes that al-Quduri gave it absolutely, but al-Kafi restricted it to one who does not own surplus nisab beyond his debt. This is the meaning of 'gharim' in the Quran (9:60): a person with debt and no means to repay. The author did not explicitly mention this condition because poverty is already a condition for all categories except the collector and the wayfarer. The text also notes a ruling from al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah that giving zakat to an indebted person is better than giving to a poor person without debt, since the debt is a greater need.

Key Terms
المديون (al-madyūn): The person who owes a debt and does not have surplus wealth beyond his needs to pay it.
الغارم (al-ghārim): A Quranic term for one burdened with debt and unable to pay; eligible for zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah, who is more deserving of zakat: a poor person or an indebted person?
A) A poor person is more deserving.
B) An indebted person is more deserving.
C) They are equal.
D) It depends on the amount of debt.

Key Takeaway
An indebted person who does not own surplus nisab is eligible for zakat and should be prioritized over a poor person without debt.

The Interpretation of 'Fi Sabil Allah' Among Hanafi Imams
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the scope of 'fi sabil Allah'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi interpretations of 'fi sabil Allah' and explain why the practical difference appears in wills and endowments rather than zakat.

Core Idea
Poverty conditions all zakat recipients, so the definition of 'fi sabil Allah' matters more in wills than in zakat.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq unpacks the Quranic phrase 'fi sabil Allah' as it pertains to zakat recipients. The Hanafi school contains multiple interpretations, but the author clarifies that the condition of poverty reduces the practical effect in zakat distribution. The key difference emerges in non-zakat contexts such as wills and endowments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic phrase and its context
The phrase 'fi sabil Allah' appears in verse 9:60 among the eight categories of zakat recipients. Identify why this category is subject to different interpretations.
2
List the three Hanafi interpretations
Abu Yusuf: those cut off for jihad (munqati' al-ghuzah). Muhammad: those cut off for hajj (munqati' al-hajj). A third opinion includes all acts of obedience, including seeking knowledge.
3
Note the condition of poverty
All interpretations require that the recipient be needy (faqir). The text states that poverty is a condition 'on all aspects' (la budda minhu).
4
Trace the practical effect (thamarah al-khilaf)
In zakat, since all are poor anyway, the difference is minimal. However, in wills and endowments where a testator says 'for the cause of Allah', the interpretation determines the distribution.
5
Recognize the author's preferred view
The author (al-Marghinani) chooses Abu Yusuf's view, meaning the relied-upon interpretation is that it refers to those cut off for jihad. But in practice, the general view of all obedience is often applied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومنقطع الغزاة) هو المراد بقوله تعالى ﴿وفي سبيل الله﴾ [التوبة : ٦٠] وهو اختيار منه لقول أبي يوسف، وعند محمد منقطع الحاج ، وقيل : طلبة العلم، واقتصر عليه في الفتاوي الظهيرية وفسره في البدائع بجميع القرب فيدخل فيه كل من سعى في طاعة الله تعالى وسبيل الخيرات إذا كان محتاجاً ا.هـ. ولا يخفى أن قيد الفقير لا بد منه على الوجوه كلها فحينئذ لا تظهر ثمرته في الزكاة وإنما تظهر في الوصايا والأوقاف كما تقدم نظيره في الفقراء والمساكين قوله : (وابن السبيل) هو المنقطع عن ماله لبعده عنه والسبيل الطريق فكل من يكون مسافراً يسمى ابن السبيل وهو غني بمكانه حتى تجب الزكاة في ماله، ويؤمر بالأداء إذا وصلت إليه يده وهو فقير يداً حتى تصرف إليه الصدقة في الحال لحاجته، كذا في الكافي. فإن قلت : منقطع الغزاة أو الحج إن لم يكن في وطنه مال فهو فقير وإلا فهو ابن السبيل، فكيف تكون الأقسام سبعة؟ قلت هو فقير إلا أنه زاد عليه بالانقطاع في عبادة الله تعالى فكان مغايراً للفقير المطلق الخالي عن هذا القيد كذا في النهاية. وفي الظهيرية : الاستقراض لابن السبيل خير من قبول الصدقة. وفي فتح القدير ولا يحل له أن يأخذ أكثر من حاجته وألحق به كل من هو غائب عن ماله وإن كان في بلده ولا يقدر عليه إلا به . وفي المحيط : وإن كان تاجراً له دين على الناس لا يقدر على أخذه ولا يجد شيئاً يحل له أخذ الزكاة لأنه فقير به
His statement: (And those cut off from the ghuzah) is what is intended by His statement 'And in the way of Allah' (9:60). And it is his choice according to the saying of Abu Yusuf. And according to Muhammad, it is those cut off from hajj. And it is said: students of knowledge. And al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah confined it to that. And al-Bada'i' interpreted it as all acts of obedience, so it includes everyone who strives in obedience to Allah and the path of good if he is needy. And it is not hidden that the condition of poverty is necessary in all aspects; therefore its benefit does not appear in zakat but appears in wills and endowments, as its like preceded in the case of the poor and needy. His statement: (And the wayfarer) is one who is cut off from his wealth due to its distance from him. 'Al-sabil' is the road, so every traveler is called ibn al-sabil. He is rich in his place, so zakat is obligatory on his wealth, and he is commanded to pay when it comes into his hand, but he is poor in hand so that sadaqah is given to him immediately for his need. Thus in al-Kafi. If you say: Those cut off from ghuzah or hajj—if he has no wealth in his homeland, he is poor; otherwise he is ibn al-sabil. So how are the categories seven? I say: He is poor, but he has the additional quality of being cut off in the obedience of Allah, so he is different from the absolute poor without this restriction. Thus in al-Nihayah. And in al-Zahiriyyah: Borrowing for the wayfarer is better than accepting charity. And in Fath al-Qadir: It is not permissible for him to take more than his need. And joined to him is everyone who is absent from his wealth even if he is in his city and cannot get it except with difficulty. And in al-Muhit: If he is a merchant who has a debt on people, he cannot collect it and has nothing, it is permissible for him to take zakat because he is poor by it.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage elaborates on two related categories: those cut off for the cause of Allah (munqati' al-ghuzah) and the wayfarer (ibn al-sabil). The author explains that 'fi sabil Allah' in the Quran is interpreted differently by the two primary students of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf says it refers to those cut off for jihad, while Muhammad says it refers to those cut off for hajj. A third opinion includes students of knowledge. However, since poverty is a condition for all recipients except the collector, the practical difference appears in wills and endowments, not in zakat. The wayfarer is one who is traveling and cut off from his wealth. He is considered rich in his place (so zakat is obligatory on his wealth at home), but poor in hand, so he can receive zakat immediately for his travel needs. The passage also notes that borrowing is better for a wayfarer than accepting charity, and he should not take more than his need. The category also includes anyone who cannot access his wealth even if he is in his city.

Key Terms
في سبيل الله (fī sabīl Allāh): The Quranic phrase for the cause of Allah; in this context, those engaged in religious service like jihad, hajj, or seeking knowledge who are in need.
ابن السبيل (ibn al-sabīl): The wayfarer; a traveler who is cut off from his wealth and in need during his journey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the difference in interpreting 'fi sabil Allah' not have a significant practical effect in zakat distribution?
A) Because the category is rarely used.
B) Because all recipients must be poor regardless of the interpretation.
C) Because the Quranic verse is unambiguous.
D) Because Abu Yusuf's view overrides others.

Key Takeaway
The practical impact of defining 'fi sabil Allah' mainly arises in wills and endowments, not in zakat distribution.

Zakat — Almsgiving

7 min
The Wayfarer (Ibn al-Sabil) as a Zakat Recipient
Explanation of the wayfarer category and its rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ibn al-sabil, state the conditions for his eligibility, and identify the ruling on borrowing versus accepting charity for him.

Core Idea
A wayfarer is rich at home but poor on the road; he may take zakat to meet his immediate need, but borrowing is better.

The second part of the passage focuses on the wayfarer (ibn al-sabil), a traveler cut off from his wealth. The author explains his unique status: he is considered rich in his hometown (hence zakat is due on his wealth) but poor during his journey, allowing him to receive zakat. The text also discusses the preference for borrowing over accepting charity, the limit of taking only what is needed, and the extension of this ruling to anyone unable to access their wealth.

Guided Path
1
Define ibn al-sabil linguistically and legally
Linguistically, 'ibn al-sabil' means 'son of the road', i.e., a traveler. Legally, it is one who is cut off from his wealth during travel. Identify the key elements: traveling, distance from wealth, need.
2
Note the dual wealth status
The wayfarer is rich in his place (ghani bi-makanihi) – zakat is obligatory on his wealth at home. But he is poor in hand (faqir yadan) – he may receive zakat for his immediate need.
3
Identify the ruling on taking charity
It is permissible for him to take zakat, but borrowing (istiqrad) is better than accepting charity (al-sadaqah). This encourages self-reliance.
4
Determine the limit of what he may take
He may only take what he needs for his journey. It is not permissible for him to take more than his need.
5
Extend the ruling to similar cases
The same ruling applies to anyone who is absent from his wealth, even if in his own city, if he cannot access it except with difficulty. Examples include a merchant with uncollectible debts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومنقطع الغزاة) هو المراد بقوله تعالى ﴿وفي سبيل الله﴾ [التوبة : ٦٠] وهو اختيار منه لقول أبي يوسف، وعند محمد منقطع الحاج ، وقيل : طلبة العلم، واقتصر عليه في الفتاوي الظهيرية وفسره في البدائع بجميع القرب فيدخل فيه كل من سعى في طاعة الله تعالى وسبيل الخيرات إذا كان محتاجاً ا.هـ. ولا يخفى أن قيد الفقير لا بد منه على الوجوه كلها فحينئذ لا تظهر ثمرته في الزكاة وإنما تظهر في الوصايا والأوقاف كما تقدم نظيره في الفقراء والمساكين قوله : (وابن السبيل) هو المنقطع عن ماله لبعده عنه والسبيل الطريق فكل من يكون مسافراً يسمى ابن السبيل وهو غني بمكانه حتى تجب الزكاة في ماله، ويؤمر بالأداء إذا وصلت إليه يده وهو فقير يداً حتى تصرف إليه الصدقة في الحال لحاجته، كذا في الكافي. فإن قلت : منقطع الغزاة أو الحج إن لم يكن في وطنه مال فهو فقير وإلا فهو ابن السبيل، فكيف تكون الأقسام سبعة؟ قلت هو فقير إلا أنه زاد عليه بالانقطاع في عبادة الله تعالى فكان مغايراً للفقير المطلق الخالي عن هذا القيد كذا في النهاية. وفي الظهيرية : الاستقراض لابن السبيل خير من قبول الصدقة. وفي فتح القدير ولا يحل له أن يأخذ أكثر من حاجته وألحق به كل من هو غائب عن ماله وإن كان في بلده ولا يقدر عليه إلا به . وفي المحيط : وإن كان تاجراً له دين على الناس لا يقدر على أخذه ولا يجد شيئاً يحل له أخذ الزكاة لأنه فقير به
His statement: (And those cut off from the ghuzah) is what is intended by His statement 'And in the way of Allah' (9:60). And it is his choice according to the saying of Abu Yusuf. And according to Muhammad, it is those cut off from hajj. And it is said: students of knowledge. And al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah confined it to that. And al-Bada'i' interpreted it as all acts of obedience, so it includes everyone who strives in obedience to Allah and the path of good if he is needy. And it is not hidden that the condition of poverty is necessary in all aspects; therefore its benefit does not appear in zakat but appears in wills and endowments, as its like preceded in the case of the poor and needy. His statement: (And the wayfarer) is one who is cut off from his wealth due to its distance from him. 'Al-sabil' is the road, so every traveler is called ibn al-sabil. He is rich in his place, so zakat is obligatory on his wealth, and he is commanded to pay when it comes into his hand, but he is poor in hand so that sadaqah is given to him immediately for his need. Thus in al-Kafi. If you say: Those cut off from ghuzah or hajj—if he has no wealth in his homeland, he is poor; otherwise he is ibn al-sabil. So how are the categories seven? I say: He is poor, but he has the additional quality of being cut off in the obedience of Allah, so he is different from the absolute poor without this restriction. Thus in al-Nihayah. And in al-Zahiriyyah: Borrowing for the wayfarer is better than accepting charity. And in Fath al-Qadir: It is not permissible for him to take more than his need. And joined to him is everyone who is absent from his wealth even if he is in his city and cannot get it except with difficulty. And in al-Muhit: If he is a merchant who has a debt on people, he cannot collect it and has nothing, it is permissible for him to take zakat because he is poor by it.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage elaborates on two related categories: those cut off for the cause of Allah (munqati' al-ghuzah) and the wayfarer (ibn al-sabil). The author explains that 'fi sabil Allah' in the Quran is interpreted differently by the two primary students of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf says it refers to those cut off for jihad, while Muhammad says it refers to those cut off for hajj. A third opinion includes students of knowledge. However, since poverty is a condition for all recipients except the collector, the practical difference appears in wills and endowments, not in zakat. The wayfarer is one who is traveling and cut off from his wealth. He is considered rich in his place (so zakat is obligatory on his wealth at home), but poor in hand, so he can receive zakat immediately for his travel needs. The passage also notes that borrowing is better for a wayfarer than accepting charity, and he should not take more than his need. The category also includes anyone who cannot access his wealth even if he is in his city.

Key Terms
ابن السبيل (ibn al-sabīl): The wayfarer; a traveler who is cut off from his wealth and in need during his journey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is it recommended for a wayfarer to borrow rather than accept charity?
A) Because borrowing is more convenient.
B) Because it preserves his dignity and self-reliance.
C) Because charity is only for the poor.
D) Because the wayfarer is rich at home.

Key Takeaway
A wayfarer's eligibility for zakat is based on immediate need, not overall wealth, and borrowing is preferred over charity.
